    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5533571480196134295">Donna Leon's riveting new novel, Doctored Evidence, follows Commissario Guido Brunetti down the winding streets of contemporary Venice as he throws open the doors of a case his superiors would rather leave closed. When a miserly spinster is found brutally murdered in her Venice apartment, police immediately suspect her Romanian housekeeper. They are certain their job is do</span>
  <span id="freeText5533571480196134295" style="display:none">Donna Leon's riveting new novel, Doctored Evidence, follows Commissario Guido Brunetti down the winding streets of contemporary Venice as he throws open the doors of a case his superiors would rather leave closed. When a miserly spinster is found brutally murdered in her Venice apartment, police immediately suspect her Romanian housekeeper. They are certain their job is done after the immigrant dies while fleeing arrest, but weeks later; a neighbor comes forward to defend the innocence of the accused. The only investigator who believes the alibi is Brunetti, who will have to go behind the backs of his superiors to vindicate the Romanian and find her employer's actual killer. As always, the indispensable hacking skills of the ever-loyal Signorina Elettra are the perfect complement to Brunetti's meticulous detective work. She discovers mysterious deposits in the old woman's bank account, but who made them? As Brunetti investigates, his wife, at home, reads him teachings on the Seven Deadly Sins. In a modern world of intrigue and nebulous morality, how do they relate to the murder at hand? Doctored Evidence is charged with suspense and evokes a contemporary Venice with Donna Leon's masterful flair.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5533571480196134295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox"><img alt="Alex is The Romance Fox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428866380p2/6663962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/243068745?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex is The Romance Fox" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox">Alex is The Romance Fox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=authors-i-o">authors-i-o</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=adventure-mystery-crime-thriller">adventure-mystery-crime-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243068745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14605415578150502446">Doctored Evidence, 13th novel in Donna Leon's Commissario Brunetti Series deals with the investigation into the brutal murder of a unpopular elderly woman. Suspicion falls upon her maid, who has vanished. When the maid is killed fleeing from the police, Brunetti takes a closer look to home....the old woman's son.<br/>We get a look into the police work in more detail and we also we see a lot more of Brunetti's relationship with his co-workers. The politics and the underhand methods that are used to un</span>
  <span id="freeText14605415578150502446" style="display:none">Doctored Evidence, 13th novel in Donna Leon's Commissario Brunetti Series deals with the investigation into the brutal murder of a unpopular elderly woman. Suspicion falls upon her maid, who has vanished. When the maid is killed fleeing from the police, Brunetti takes a closer look to home....the old woman's son.<br />We get a look into the police work in more detail and we also we see a lot more of Brunetti's relationship with his co-workers. The politics and the underhand methods that are used to undermine the work the good cops are doing in seeing the bad guys brought to justice.<br />Brunetti's relationship with Paola, his wife, continues to amaze me....I enjoy their interaction.....<br /><blockquote>
  <b>“There’s a chapter here,” she said, pointing at the page she’d been reading, “on the Seven Deadly Sins.”<br />…(B)y thinking eschatologically,’ he said: ‘Death. Judgement. Heaven. Hell.’<br />‘You don’t really believe in any of that, do you?’ asked an astonished Paola.<br />‘There are times when it would be nice,’ he said…</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I enjoyed this one...but not one of my favorite in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14605415578150502446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5061568103542985404">This is possibly one of the most boring Brunetti books yet, but I'm upping it a star because of the neat tie-in with the title at the end. Donna Leon dropped the mic on that one and walked away, brushing her shoulders off. Some things I enjoyed in this installment:<br/><br/>- Signora Gismondi! I would read her diary. The idea that she met her lover in London before coming home to her Venetian apartment to cook a pasta with garlic and eggplant fills me with envy.<br/>- Vianello and Brunetti go out for lunch and</span>
  <span id="freeText5061568103542985404" style="display:none">This is possibly one of the most boring Brunetti books yet, but I'm upping it a star because of the neat tie-in with the title at the end. Donna Leon dropped the mic on that one and walked away, brushing her shoulders off. Some things I enjoyed in this installment:<br /><br />- Signora Gismondi! I would read her diary. The idea that she met her lover in London before coming home to her Venetian apartment to cook a pasta with garlic and eggplant fills me with envy.<br />- Vianello and Brunetti go out for lunch and the restaurants are closed because it's too hot, so they sulk because their wives have made pasta and they've missed it. Direct quote: "They returned to the Questura, oppressed by the still-growing heat and their mutual resentment at having had to lunch on sandwiches." #venetianproblems<br />- Patta appeared only once, but I appreciated Brunetti's reflections on training a new southerner to head the department. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He can't go to Interpol! I haven't had enough outfit descriptions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- The entire Questura auguring the sky to see if the weather is nice enough for the department meeting to be cancelled was a great image.<br /><br />This list is not nearly long enough, which is probably because I found the Seven Deadly Sins theme not particularly palatable. Brunetti Hulks out a couple too many times in this book. I'm also here for the Vianello/Brunetti bromance, so when that is threatened I am immediately suspicious.<br /><br />Also, aside from the great scene where Signora Gismondi cooks, there is not enough food in this book. Paola only cooks a couple of times, and the other times she's letting Brunetti know the meals that he's missing out on. (What about the meals that I'M missing out on, Leon??) </span>
  <a data-text-id="5061568103542985404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13671227560988420292">The first half gave some excellent characterizations for the murder victim and her home health worker. And also some intense incite into Scarpa's mode of thinking and sycophant habits.<br/><br/>But the banking minutia, the habits of the relatives of the deceased, and all their subsequent money trailing associations- that all was BELOW the 3 star level. Not only boring, but when Guido returned home now and again, there was Paola discussion that, to me, verged on obnoxious. And not just for Paola's input ei</span>
  <span id="freeText13671227560988420292" style="display:none">The first half gave some excellent characterizations for the murder victim and her home health worker. And also some intense incite into Scarpa's mode of thinking and sycophant habits.<br /><br />But the banking minutia, the habits of the relatives of the deceased, and all their subsequent money trailing associations- that all was BELOW the 3 star level. Not only boring, but when Guido returned home now and again, there was Paola discussion that, to me, verged on obnoxious. And not just for Paola's input either. Such elitist opinions about how much money is "enough" to save! Or what greed is? But it was more than that, both of them seemed like pills for what they experience, hold, own etc.<br /><br />At times in this one with the corruption levels and the assumptions of crooked job bids taken as a given, I found that the judgmental quality of the Brunetti's (all of them) became off-putting by comparison. And especially upon deciding what English ideas are vile or noble- or sounding like one while being the other. And at the same time venting cynicism themselves. <br /><br />At times I feel that Donna Leon gets all her own politico venting and spewing in regardless of the story line. In this one, she sure it. <br /><br />In the end, the perp was along a completely different alley. One as pompous as some of the Brunetti's conversations.<br /><br />This one has next to no humor. And a dead pet. Not one I would recommend.</span>

<div id="review_3029463460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029463460" />
    <a title="Dorothy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/931455-dorothy"><img alt="Dorothy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581454753p2/931455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029463460?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorothy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorothy" href="/user/show/931455-dorothy">Dorothy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19181001-doctored-evidence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=modern-day-mysteries">modern-day-mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=police-procedurals">police-procedurals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029463460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6627324748908021837">I haven't visited Venice and the Brunetti family for a while, so let's hop a vaporetto and check out what the good Commissario Brunetti is up to.<br/><br/>Well, it seems he's up to the same old thing - fighting the good fight (usually a losing fight) against the endemic corruption in Venetian and Italian society. This is the thirteenth in Donna Leon's popular series and it was published in 2004, so we are slowly getting closer to the current day.<br/><br/>The case that is drawing Brunetti's attention this time arou</span>
  <span id="freeText6627324748908021837" style="display:none">I haven't visited Venice and the Brunetti family for a while, so let's hop a vaporetto and check out what the good Commissario Brunetti is up to.<br /><br />Well, it seems he's up to the same old thing - fighting the good fight (usually a losing fight) against the endemic corruption in Venetian and Italian society. This is the thirteenth in Donna Leon's popular series and it was published in 2004, so we are slowly getting closer to the current day.<br /><br />The case that is drawing Brunetti's attention this time around is the brutal murder of an old woman in her apartment. The murder had happened a few weeks before and had been quickly "solved" by the odious Lieutenant Scarpa. It was determined that the woman's Romanian carer had killed her and then she herself had been killed when struck by a train while fleeing police. Brunetti's fatuous superior, Patta, is, of course, delighted with the quick result.<br /><br />Then a neighbor who has been out of the country contacts the police to provide an alibi for the Romanian. She knows that she could not possibly have killed her employer. Scarpa is not happy and doesn't want to hear it, so he passes her off to Brunetti. Brunetti listens to her story and believes her. He decides to investigate but will have to do it on the sly since Patta considers the case closed.<br /><br />He soon learns that the woman was universally despised and there are any number of people who might have wanted to kill her. As he and Vianello and Signorina Elettra dig into the background and finances of the victim, searching for a possible motive, they find several bank accounts with a substantial sum of money. Money is always a good motive, but Brunetti suspects something more personal and keeps digging.<br /><br />While he digs, of course, he still goes home for lunch and dinner each day, prepared by his gourmet cook wife, Paola, and enjoys his meals with her and their son and daughter, now teenagers. The family's interactions around the dinner table are always some of the best moments of these books. His conversations with his wife keep him grounded and give him and the reader a lot to think about - in this case, it's the Seven Deadly Sins!<br /><br />Maybe the deadliest sin of all is pride and the fear of being shamed. It's the cause of much misery in the world.<br /><br />The play on words behind the title of the book becomes clear near the end and brings a smile. Clever plotting and a quick and undemanding read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6627324748908021837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9755497976326583162">One of Leon's unforgettable beginnings - "She was an old cow and he hated her." - proceeds to an equally terse and memorable conclusion. Along the way, the Scarpa intrigue becomes a confrontation, and Brunetti examines the Seven Deadly Sins in the light of modern justice. A repulsive victim, a mediocre "victim," not to mention several examples of true virtue, including a Romanian caregiver and a golden retriever. One of Leon's best. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025593097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11262703387308505764">Another Venetian mystery from Donna Leon, with its usual share of corruption, delicious food, and problematic policemen. As ever, Leon is exceptional at conveying a sense of place, especially given the small geographic area that is Venice. I liked the red herrings, and didn't guess the culprit until the end, which is what I want from a mystery novel. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_116542337" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116542337" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116542337?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=detective-fiction">detective-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116542337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7865435673575196415">After the raging disappointment that was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1068886.Through_a_Glass_Darkly_Ethnic_Semiosis_in_American_Literature' title='Through a Glass Darkly Ethnic Semiosis in American Literature by William Boelhower' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through a Glass Darkly</a>, I'm tempted to give this book a higher rating than it deserves based just on how much better it was. So I'll settle for three stars, which in my mind translates to "pretty good, I guess." <br/><br/>The truth is I'm getting a little bored with Commissario Brunetti. So many little things are starting to grate at me: the way he lovingly describes every article of clothing and jewelry his smokin' colleague Signorina Elettra is wearing every damn</span>
  <span id="freeText7865435673575196415" style="display:none">After the raging disappointment that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1068886.Through_a_Glass_Darkly_Ethnic_Semiosis_in_American_Literature" title="Through a Glass Darkly Ethnic Semiosis in American Literature by William Boelhower" rel="nofollow noopener">Through a Glass Darkly</a>, I'm tempted to give this book a higher rating than it deserves based just on how much better it was. So I'll settle for three stars, which in my mind translates to "pretty good, I guess." <br /><br />The truth is I'm getting a little bored with Commissario Brunetti. So many little things are starting to grate at me: the way he lovingly describes every article of clothing and jewelry his smokin' colleague Signorina Elettra is wearing every damn day, his constant mind-bitching whenever he's so busy he can't go home for lunch and spend an hour eating a fabulous home-cooked meal (honestly, he has to eat lunch in a restaurant once and <i>will not shut up</i> about how he has to lower himself to <i>sandwiches</i>), and of course Leon's half-assed attempts to connect every crime to some classical work of art. This time it's the Seven Deadly Sins, and I won't even bother to explain the connection because it barely works and is kind of stupid. <br /><br />Now we're really getting into the nitpicking, but this part just drove me crazy so I'm going to quote it. So Brunetti is thinking about Signorina Elettra and how it annoys him that she wasn't in the office once when he needed her. The following passage is recorded exactly as it appears in the book, with nothing omitted.<br />"That in turn provoked a flash of shame at the moment's rage he'd felt at her absence. Like Otello, he had a lieutenant who could corrupt his best feelings.<br /><br />As though forewarned that today she was to play Desdemona, Signorina Elettra wore a loose dress of gossamer white linen, her hair hanging loose down her back." <br /><br />But...Leon, you <i>just said</i> she was Cassio, not Desdemona. Or I am reading something wrong? Either way, it's lazy narration and it annoyed me a lot more than it should have. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7865435673575196415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_629712964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/629712964" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/108416-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351512283p2/108416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/629712964?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/108416-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629712964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1249456115631842536">Donna Leon is the perfect author for serial addicts. She has created a great set of characters; sets her books in a wonderful city (Venice) for the readers to explore; and gives a moderate dose of philosophy or morality for us to ponder. I love her! Perhaps the only reason I have given this book three stars, not four, is that I've read three or four of her mysteries now and have high expectations---I know she'll be good, so I am not gob-smacked by how wonderful the books are.<br/><br/>If any readers recal</span>
  <span id="freeText1249456115631842536" style="display:none">Donna Leon is the perfect author for serial addicts. She has created a great set of characters; sets her books in a wonderful city (Venice) for the readers to explore; and gives a moderate dose of philosophy or morality for us to ponder. I love her! Perhaps the only reason I have given this book three stars, not four, is that I've read three or four of her mysteries now and have high expectations---I know she'll be good, so I am not gob-smacked by how wonderful the books are.<br /><br />If any readers recall the series of "business" mysteries by Emma Lathen (featuring a bank executive as detective) they will be familiar with the notion of an extraordinary secretary who has the not-so-subtle knack of making her superior look less capable than she. Leon's books feature the excellent Signorina Elettra who is impossibly chic, tremendously capable, and always brings a smile to my face. She is critical to the solution of all the murders and equally important to the pleasurable camaraderie of the police staff.<br /><br />Enough of this---I have two more Donna Leon mysteries to read this weekend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1249456115631842536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16450999671572250120" style="display:none">I enjoy reading about the Brunetti family, to hear about Raffi and Chiara and the banter between Paola and Guido. I envy their kids sometimes about what food Paola cooks for them. Half of the time I think about diving into traditional Italian cooking and the other half of the time my stomach grumbles angrily and wants to be fed. I have not gotten myself one of the meals Paolo cooks though. <br /><br />The mystery can easily become a side kick, though I think looking at it this way is strange. The character development is the best part of Leon's books. <br /><br />When I finished the book I remembered vaguely that I watched the series on TV ages (years) ago. <br /><br />I thought it was tragic that we think about the Rom or Roma or Gypsies in such a negative way and the more they and their lifestyle was thematised in the book, I got sadder and angrier. <span id="freeTextContainer6529887279314105944">An old woman beaten to death in her home, her maid is on the run, and all is not what it seems. Another intriguing Brunetti mystery where he has to manipulate his political foe to go beyond what appears to the truth to actually finding the truth.<br/><br/>An old, bitter, nasty woman is found beaten in her home; so many suspects as it appears she was hated by everyone who came into her path.   <span id="freeText6529887279314105944" style="display:none">An old woman beaten to death in her home, her maid is on the run, and all is not what it seems. Another intriguing Brunetti mystery where he has to manipulate his political foe to go beyond what appears to the truth to actually finding the truth.<br /><br />An old, bitter, nasty woman is found beaten in her home; so many suspects as it appears she was hated by everyone who came into her path. I don't know Italian laws, but I always chuckle when Brunetti casually does something that would appear to be, shall we say, not entirely really legal. Breaking into the old ladies home to go through her stuff, utilizing hackers to find information (although to fair, the hackers do work for the police) - but he always finds his killer.<br /><br />I love his relationship with his wife and kids and as always, the description of the food he eats makes me so incredibly hungry. Never disappointed with a Brunetti murder.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602522238" />
    <a title="The Book Shelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31416418-the-book-shelf"><img alt="The Book Shelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400181362p2/31416418.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602522238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15527678191691066399">This is the fifth or sixth book by Donna Leon that I have read. Her chief detective, Commissario Guido Brunetti, fascinates me. He is well-read, loves his wife and children, is diligent in his investigations and has a slightly cynical attitude toward the way business is conducted in his home city of Venice. When I read these books I feel like I have been to the city and have absorbed the ambiance of it. The relationship between he and his wife, Paola, is a mature one built on love and respect. I</span>
  <span id="freeText15527678191691066399" style="display:none">This is the fifth or sixth book by Donna Leon that I have read. Her chief detective, Commissario Guido Brunetti, fascinates me. He is well-read, loves his wife and children, is diligent in his investigations and has a slightly cynical attitude toward the way business is conducted in his home city of Venice. When I read these books I feel like I have been to the city and have absorbed the ambiance of it. The relationship between he and his wife, Paola, is a mature one built on love and respect. I hope that Ms. Leon continues to write this series - it is a treat to read her books.</span>

<div id="review_2591851092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591851092" />
    <a title="Bonnieb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11823363-bonnieb"><img alt="Bonnieb" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591851092?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnieb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnieb" href="/user/show/11823363-bonnieb">Bonnieb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11823363-bonnieb?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591851092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13645279220320244090"> Another in the Commissario Guido Brunetti mystery series. This is the sixth I have read and with each one, I am more sure than ever that I would not ever wish to live in Venice. Leon seems to make her protagonist, Brunetti, more cynical in every new story I read: a police commissioner who has a political hack for a boss, incompetent and crooked police around him, and little hope for the laws, trust, processes of the ‘system’ within Venice. He works AROUND the law as much as he works with it. In</span>
  <span id="freeText13645279220320244090" style="display:none"> Another in the Commissario Guido Brunetti mystery series. This is the sixth I have read and with each one, I am more sure than ever that I would not ever wish to live in Venice. Leon seems to make her protagonist, Brunetti, more cynical in every new story I read: a police commissioner who has a political hack for a boss, incompetent and crooked police around him, and little hope for the laws, trust, processes of the ‘system’ within Venice. He works AROUND the law as much as he works with it. In this story, the case he solves is not even his, but he realizes that an innocent person has been blamed and the case closed when she most likely did not commit the crime. He must solve it behind the responsible lieutenant’s back. The way of life and culture of Venice continues to both shine and show its dark side. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13645279220320244090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ruby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8259858-ruby"><img alt="Ruby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332105241p2/8259858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Ruby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruby" href="/user/show/8259858-ruby">Ruby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3031069787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6907682939017646256">Another entertaining mystery in the Commissario Brunetti series. This time, an elderly woman who is hated by pretty much everyone who came into contact with her is murdered. There appears to be an obvious suspect, who dies before being arrested, so the case appears to be resolved. But Commissario Brunetti, as usual, isn't buying it, and he, along with his faithful team, figures out the real murderer and why.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9504242996972554763">Having read so many of Donna Leon's mysteries set in Venice, Italy, I can offer testimony to the amazing way she draws you into the wonders, banalities, romance, cuisine, family values, government and of course, police procedure as revealed through the eyes of her wonderful Commisario Guido Brunetti. Please treat yourself to her books. This one is excellent and won't let you go.</span>

<div id="review_208654720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208654720" />
    <a title="Jennifer Blake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6299057-jennifer-blake"><img alt="Jennifer Blake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315996966p2/6299057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208654720?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Blake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Blake" href="/user/show/6299057-jennifer-blake">Jennifer Blake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6299057-jennifer-blake?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208654720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11212434378504547274">A housebound old woman with a mean temper and nasty habits is brutality murdered, and no one cares. No one, that is, except Commissario Brunetti. So begins DOCTORED EVIDENCE, an intriguing study of murder Italian style, one that explores the ramifications of motive, also the uneasy fit of modern murder into the list of Seven Deadly Sins. Brunetti is in fine form as he threads his way through the labyrinthine streets and waterways of Venice--which serve as a metaphor for tangled Italian law and p</span>
  <span id="freeText11212434378504547274" style="display:none">A housebound old woman with a mean temper and nasty habits is brutality murdered, and no one cares. No one, that is, except Commissario Brunetti. So begins DOCTORED EVIDENCE, an intriguing study of murder Italian style, one that explores the ramifications of motive, also the uneasy fit of modern murder into the list of Seven Deadly Sins. Brunetti is in fine form as he threads his way through the labyrinthine streets and waterways of Venice--which serve as a metaphor for tangled Italian law and politics—to right a wrong. A disillusioned knight in a well-cut Italian suit, armored in irony, balancing anger and due concern for his stomach, he fights always for justice. Sometimes using the system, sometimes going beyond it, Brunetti wields every resource at his command to force the killer out of hiding.<br /><br />There’s no furious action and few thrilling chases in Leon’s Venetian mysteries. Like ancient Greek and Roman dramas, they grind their inevitable way through human pride and stupidity, greed and frailty to reach an end that may or may not be entirely just. Yet I enjoy the stories for their portrait of a philosophical man of fiercely-protected sensibilities pitted against the evils of the world—also for their “Aha!” moments when something recalls the Venice I've known as an awestruck tourist. I like their character interactions, their small mysteries and secrets that are never fully revealed, and especially their atmosphere that’s so strong I can smell the dank canals, taste the garlic, savor the espresso and pastries. I just enjoy them, period.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11212434378504547274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2085903909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085903909" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7669076-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388107500p2/7669076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085903909?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/7669076-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7669076-deb?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7669076-deb?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7669076-deb?shelf=italy">italy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7669076-deb?shelf=venice">venice</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085903909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16671569463310397285">In this outing, Guido Brunetti returns from a vacation to find a 3-week-old murder, supposedly solved, has suddenly gained renewed life. The thorn in Brunetti's side is Lieutenant Scarpa, the much-despised non-Venetian inspector who is the pet of Vice-Questore Patta. Scarpa made up his mind that a Romanian caretaker killed an old woman, pursued the Romanian, and declared the case closed when the woman died fleeing the police. Now a new witness has come forward insisting the Romanian woman could </span>
  <span id="freeText16671569463310397285" style="display:none">In this outing, Guido Brunetti returns from a vacation to find a 3-week-old murder, supposedly solved, has suddenly gained renewed life. The thorn in Brunetti's side is Lieutenant Scarpa, the much-despised non-Venetian inspector who is the pet of Vice-Questore Patta. Scarpa made up his mind that a Romanian caretaker killed an old woman, pursued the Romanian, and declared the case closed when the woman died fleeing the police. Now a new witness has come forward insisting the Romanian woman could not have committed the crime. <br />Brunetti and his team quietly pursue the real culprit; but the fun for fans of this series is watching Brunetti navigate the politics of a corrupt system, manage a team alarmingly inclined to bypass legalities to find information, and still maintain some semblance of ethics himself. That sounds darker than this book actually is; one of things I enjoy most about these characters is the frequent humor and glimpses of the family lives of the detectives. Try Donna Leon if you want to get invested in a good mystery series with rich characters and a wonderful sense of place. Venice is one of the regular characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16671569463310397285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478144-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450473p2/1478144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1587201851?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/1478144-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099536550" href="/book/show/11543647-doctored-evidence">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1587201851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer41308829656555726">An old woman whom everyone loathed (and with good cause) is found brutally murdered. When her Romanian paid companion seemingly goes on the run and then, on being approached by the cops, falls in front of a train, everyone assumes the case is over -- everyone except Commissario Brunetti, because it's to him that the neighbor speaks who knows the Romanian companion couldn't have done it . . .<br/><br/>My problem with this series is that I'm very fond of Andrea Camilleri's novels, of which these seem pale i</span>
  <span id="freeText41308829656555726" style="display:none">An old woman whom everyone loathed (and with good cause) is found brutally murdered. When her Romanian paid companion seemingly goes on the run and then, on being approached by the cops, falls in front of a train, everyone assumes the case is over -- everyone except Commissario Brunetti, because it's to him that the neighbor speaks who knows the Romanian companion couldn't have done it . . .<br /><br />My problem with this series is that I'm very fond of Andrea Camilleri's novels, of which these seem pale imitations. This one was a pleasant enough read, but it never set my blood coursing. Even if for the wrong reasons, I spotted the guilty party the moment that party came on stage, which didn't help. I imagine that, for Donna Leon's legions of fans, this'll be another fine entry in the series; if you're one of the few curmudgeonly dissenters like me, it's just a moderately amiable way to pass the time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="41308829656555726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186369851?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg Morden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg Morden" href="/user/show/16310354-meg-morden">Meg Morden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099446750" href="/book/show/372714.Doctored_Evidence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16310354-meg-morden?shelf=venice">venice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16310354-meg-morden?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186369851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5873486799162274306">The murder of an old woman takes place when Brunetti is away on holiday with his family in Ireland and so the case is handled by Lieutenant Scarpa. It appears to be an open-and-set case with the Romanian maid seen as guilty due to her precipitous escape home. But when a neigbour of the dead woman returns from a trip to a language course in London, and presents new evidence, Brunetti secretly reopens the case.<br/>The case is set against the backdrop of Brunetti's wife Paola reading their daughter's r</span>
  <span id="freeText5873486799162274306" style="display:none">The murder of an old woman takes place when Brunetti is away on holiday with his family in Ireland and so the case is handled by Lieutenant Scarpa. It appears to be an open-and-set case with the Romanian maid seen as guilty due to her precipitous escape home. But when a neigbour of the dead woman returns from a trip to a language course in London, and presents new evidence, Brunetti secretly reopens the case.<br />The case is set against the backdrop of Brunetti's wife Paola reading their daughter's religious studies book and Brunetti explores the motives in relation to the 7 deadly sins: pride, lust, greed, sloth, gluttony, jealousy and wrath and how in this modern age they are not considered as deadly as before.<br />We get to see a bit more of Lieutenant Scarpa in this book and see that he is really a nasty piece of work. Brunetti has to go toe to toe with him and may have to pay the consequences in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5873486799162274306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2189893971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189893971" />
    <a title="Jane Glen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7439172-jane-glen"><img alt="Jane Glen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326678230p2/7439172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189893971?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Glen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Glen" href="/user/show/7439172-jane-glen">Jane Glen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189893971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer917470202989098618">I love these books and I always learn something new about Venice. I note that this author has a very ambiguous relationship with organized religion. There always seem to be a few barbs inserted here and there through the voice of Paola, while Brunetti himself is more ambivalent. This is the sentence that caught me totally off guard. "Brunetti, a man of sorrows and afflicted with grief, said..... "First of all, this is not an accurate description of Brunetti's character as shown in the other book</span>
  <span id="freeText917470202989098618" style="display:none">I love these books and I always learn something new about Venice. I note that this author has a very ambiguous relationship with organized religion. There always seem to be a few barbs inserted here and there through the voice of Paola, while Brunetti himself is more ambivalent. This is the sentence that caught me totally off guard. "Brunetti, a man of sorrows and afflicted with grief, said..... "First of all, this is not an accurate description of Brunetti's character as shown in the other books and it is a quote from Isaiah 53:3, a prophetic chapter referring to the coming of the Messiah, Jesus Christ. "He is despised and rejected of men, a man of sorrows and acquainted with grief." How odd she would choose to quote from a book that she seems to have rejected. I just found it interesting and a source of wonderment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="917470202989098618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2581138881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581138881" />
    <a title="Jeanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12190587-jeanne"><img alt="Jeanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345846885p2/12190587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581138881?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanne" href="/user/show/12190587-jeanne">Jeanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581138881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5839577023936814434">Who killed the nasty old woman? Was it the Romanian aide that Lieutenant Scarpa assumed when he quickly closed the case? Was it the witness who turned up 2 weeks later to clear the Romanian woman? Was it the mentally impaired niece who inherited everything? Was it the attorney who quickly moved the old woman’s questionable bank accounts offshore?<br/><br/>No to all the above. Commissario Brunetti and Vianello are particularly frustrated by this case. The incompetent Lieutenant Scarpi continually interfere</span>
  <span id="freeText5839577023936814434" style="display:none">Who killed the nasty old woman? Was it the Romanian aide that Lieutenant Scarpa assumed when he quickly closed the case? Was it the witness who turned up 2 weeks later to clear the Romanian woman? Was it the mentally impaired niece who inherited everything? Was it the attorney who quickly moved the old woman’s questionable bank accounts offshore?<br /><br />No to all the above. Commissario Brunetti and Vianello are particularly frustrated by this case. The incompetent Lieutenant Scarpi continually interferes. It’s particularly satisfying when Brunetti threatens Scarpi. Signorina Elettra is quite interesting in this book as she trains Vianello in her methods of discovering evidence. <br /><br />The real killer was quite a surprise to everyone. Of course the identity of the killer is discovered only by accident when Brunetti stumbles and falls during a search for evidence</span>

<div id="review_489264492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489264492" />
    <a title="Siri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3841240-siri"><img alt="Siri" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489264492?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siri" href="/user/show/3841240-siri">Siri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489264492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer498048409704378236">I read this one a couple of years ago but had forgotten the plot line. On our trip back from California we listened to it, and I thoroughly enjoyed it. Something that came through more on the audio than reading was the humor I found myself laughing out load at several of Brunetti's comments. As with most of her stories, the plot moves slowly but is rich with characters, red herrings and brick walls. Which is probably a more realistic picture of how cases get solved.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6RKQSJlid4V7X2p9Iepki8RiRHynumuTCpjaVhPf7ssTiJ7p6eEyu2cExrLW4IKu/lJuSr+HKxy0zygejqlT/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Amelia Kennerly is worried, too, when her holiday is interrupted by the news that she has been appointed executrix for a great-aunt she only met once. Now she is in charge of executing a number of inconvenient requests from her late Aunt Octavia. But when Octavia Garamond\'s house is broken into and her papers ransacked, it begins to occur to all concerned that perhaps her written requests were not simply the ramblings of a senile old lady, but the actions of a woman in fear of her life. Inspector Sloane, aided (as it were) by Constable Crosby, finds himself facing an inexplicable puzzle. Who would want to harm a quiet eighty-year-old woman? He must dig deep into Garamond\'s past, both personal and professional, to uncover the key to a long-kept secret and reveal the sinister truth behind her tragic death. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9264660861280869497">Donna Leon (born September 29, 1942, in Montclair, New Jersey) is an American author of a series of crime novels set in Venice and featuring the fictional hero Commissario Guido Brunetti.<br/><br/>Donna Leon has lived in Venice for over twenty-five years. She has worked as a lecturer in English Literature for the University of Maryland University College - Europe (UMUC-Europe) in Italy, then as a Professor </span>
  <span id="freeText9264660861280869497" style="display:none">Donna Leon (born September 29, 1942, in Montclair, New Jersey) is an American author of a series of crime novels set in Venice and featuring the fictional hero Commissario Guido Brunetti.<br /><br />Donna Leon has lived in Venice for over twenty-five years. She has worked as a lecturer in English Literature for the University of Maryland University College - Europe (UMUC-Europe) in Italy, then as a Professor from 1981 to 1999 at the american military base of Vicenza (Italy) and a writer. <br /><br />Her crime novels are all situated in or near Venice. They are written in English and translated into many foreign languages, although not, by her request, into Italian. Her ninth Brunetti novel, Friends in High Places, won the Crime Writers' Association Silver Dagger in 2000.<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/50419-commissario-brunetti" rel="nofollow noopener">Commissario Brunetti</a></span>
